neck and shoulders whose whiteness they delightfully set off. Then the<br>
luxuriant swell of flesh that rose from the small of his back, and<br>
terminates its double cope at where the thighs are set off, perfectly<br>
dazzled one with its watery glistening gloss.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;By this time I was so affected by this inward involution of<br>
sentiments, so softened by this sight, that now, betrayed into a sudden<br>
transition from extreme fears to extreme desires, I found these last so<br>
strong upon me, the heat of the weather too perhaps conspiring to exalt<br>
their rage, that nature almost fainted under them. Not that I so much<br>
as knew precisely what was wanting to me: my only thought was, that so<br>
sweet a creature, as this youth seemed to me, could only make me happy;<br>
but then, the little likelihood there was of compassing an acquaintance<br>
with him, or perhaps of ever seeing him again, dashed my desires, and<br>
turned them into torments. I was still gazing, with all the powers of<br>
my sight, on this bewitching object, when, in an instant, down he went.<br>
I had heard of such things as a cramp seizing on even the best<br>
swimmers, and occasioning their being drowned; and imagining this so<br>
sudden eclipse to be owing to it, the inconceivable fondness this<br>
unknown lad had given birth to, distracted me with the most killing<br>
terrors; insomuch, that my concern giving the wings, I flew to the<br>
door, opened it, ran down to the canal, guided thither by the madness<br>
of my fears for him, and the intense desire of being an instrument to<br>
save him, though I was ignorant how, or by what means to effect it: but<br>
was it for fears, and a passion so sudden as mine, to reason! All this<br>
took up scarce the space of a few moments. I had then just life enough<br>
to reach the green borders of the waterpiece, where wildly looking<br>
round for the young man, and missing him still, my fright and concern<br>
sunk me down in a deep swoon, which must have lasted me some time; for<br>
I did not come to myself, till I was roused out of it by a sense of<br>
pain that pierced me to the vitals, and awaked me to the the most<br>
surprising circumstance of finding myself not only in the arms of this<br>
very young gentleman I had been so solicitous to save; but taken at<br>
such an advantage in my unresisting condition, that he had actually<br>
completed his entrance into me so far, that weakened as I was by all<br>
the preceding conflicts of mind I had suffered, and struck dumb by the<br>
violence of my surprise, I had neither the power to cry out, nor the<br>
strength to disengage myself from his strenuous embraces, before,<br>
urging his point, he had forced his way and completely triumphed over<br>
my virginity, as he might now as well see by the streams of blood that<br>
followed his drawing out, as he had felt by the difficulties he had met<br>
with consummating his penetration. But the sight of the blood, and the<br>
sense of my condition, had (as he told me afterwards), since the<br>
ungovernable rage of his passion was somewhat appeased, now wrought so<br>
far on him, that at all risks, even of the worst consequences, he could<br>
not find in his heart to leave me, and make off, which he might easily<br>
have done. I still lay all discomposed in bleeding ruin, palpitating,<br>
speechless, unable to get off, and frightened, and fluttering like a<br>
poor wounded partridge, and ready to faint away again at the sense of<br>
what had befallen me. The young gentleman was by me, kneeling, kissing<br>
my hand, and with tears in his eyes, beseeching me to forgive him, and<br>
offering all the reparation in his power. It is certain that could I,<br>
at the instant of regaining my senses, have called out, or taken the<br>
bloodiest revenge, I would not be stuck at it; the violation was<br>
attended too with such aggravating circumstances, though he was<br>
ignorant of them, since it was to my concern for the preservation of<br>
his life, that I owed my ruin.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;But how quick is the shift of passions from one extreme to another!<br>
and how little are they acquainted with the human heart who dispute it!<br>
I could not see this amiable criminal, so suddenly the first object of<br>
my love, and as suddenly of my just hate, on his knees, bedewing my<br>
hands with his tears, without relenting. He was still stark-naked, but<br>
my modesty had been already too much wounded, in essentials, to be so<br>
much shocked as I should have otherwise been with appearances only; in<br>
short, my anger ebbed so fast, and the tide of love returned so strong<br>
upon me, that I felt it a point of my own happiness to forgive him. The<br>
reproaches I made him were murmured in so soft a tone, my eyes met his<br>
with such glances, expressing more languor than resentment, that he<br>
could not but presume his forgiveness was at no desperate distance; but<br>
still he would not quit his posture of submission, till I had<br>
pronounced his pardon in form; which after the most fervent entreaties,<br>
protestations, and promises, I had not the power to withhold. On which,<br>
with the utmost marks of a fear of again offending, he ventured to kiss<br>
my lips, which I neither declined nor resented: but on my mild<br>
expostulation with him upon the barbarity of his treatment, he<br>
explained the mystery of my ruin, if not entirely to the clearance, at<br>
least much to the alleviation of his guilt, in the eyes of a judge so<br>
partial in his favour as I was grown.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;It seems that the circumstance of his going down, or sinking, which in<br>
my extreme ignorance I had mistaken for something very fatal, was no<br>
other than a trick of diving, which I had not ever heard, or at least<br>
attended o, the mention of: and he was so long-breathed at it, that in<br>
the few moments in which I ran out to save him, he had not yet emerged,<br>
before I fell into the swoon, in which, as he rose, seeing me extended<br>
on the bank, his first idea was, that some young woman was upon some<br>
design of frolic or diversion with him, for he knew I could not have<br>
fallen asleep there without his having seen me before: agreebly to<br>
which notion he had ventured to approach, and finding me without sign<br>
of life, and still perplexed as he was what to think of the adventure,<br>
he took me in his arms at all hazards, and carried me into the<br>
summer-house, of which he observed the door open: there he laid me down<br>
on the couch, and tried, as he protested in good faith, by several<br>
means to bring me to myself again, till fired, as he said, beyond all<br>
bearing by the sight and touch of several parts of me, which were<br>
unguardedly exposed to him, he could no longer govern his passion; and<br>
the less, as he was not quite sure that his first idea of this swoon<br>
being a feint, was not the very truth of the case; seduced then by this<br>
flattering notion, and overcome by the present, as he styled them,<br>
super-human temptations, combined with the solitude and seeming<br>
security of the attempt, he was not enough his own master not to make<br>
it. Leaving me then just only whilst he fastened the door, he returned<br>
with redoubled eagerness to his prey: when, finding me still entranced,<br>
he ventured to place me as he pleased, whilst I felt, no more than the<br>
dead, what he was about, till the pain he put me to roused me just in<br>
time enough to be witness of a triumph I was not able to defeat, and<br>
now scarce regretted: for as he talked, the tone of his voice sounded,<br>
methought, so sweetly in my ears, the sensible nearness of so new and<br>
interesting an object to me, wrought so powerfully upon me, that, in<br>
the rising perception of things in a new and pleasing light, I lost all<br>
sense of the past injury. The young gentleman soon discerned the<br>
symptoms of a reconciliation in my softened looks, and hastening to<br>
receive the seal of it from my lips, pressed them tenderly to pass his<br>
pardon in the return of a kiss so melting fiery, that the impression of<br>
it being carried to my heart, and thence to my new discovered sphere of<br>
Venus, I was melted into a softness that could refuse him nothing. When<br>
now he managed his caresses and endearments so artfully, as to<br>
insinuate the most soothing consolations for the past pain and the most<br>
pleasing expectations of future pleasure, but whilst mere modesty kept<br>
my eyes from seeing his and rather declined them, I had a glimpse of<br>
that instrument of mischief which was now, obviously even to me, who<br>
had scarce had snatches of a comparative observation of it, resuming<br>
its capacity to renew it, and grew greatly alarming with its increase<br>
of size, as he bore it no doubt designedly, hard and stiff against one<br>
of my hands carelessly dropt; but then he employed such tender<br>
prefacing, such winning progressions, that my returning passion of<br>
desire being now so strongly prompted by the engaging circumstances of<br>
the sight and incendiary touch of his naked glowing beauties, I yield<br>
at length at the force of the present impressions, and he obtained of<br>
my tacit blushing consent all the gratifications of pleasure left in<br>
the power of my poor person to bestow, after he had cropt its richest<br>
flower, during my suspension of life, and abilities to guard it.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;Here, according to the rule laid down, I should stop; but I am so much<br>
in notion, that I could not if I would. I shall only add, however, that<br>
I got home without the least discovery, or suspicion of what had<br>
happened. I met my young ravisher several times after, whom I now<br>
passionately loved and who, though not of age to claim a small but<br>
independent fortune, would have married me; but as the accident that<br>
prevented it, and its consequences, which threw me on the public,<br>
contain matters too moving and serious to introduce at present, I cut<br>
short here.&rdquo;<br>
<br>
Louisa, the brunette whom I mentioned at first, now took her turn to<br>
treat the company with her history. I have already hinted to you the<br>
graces of her person, than which nothing could be more exquisitely<br>
touching; I repeat touching, as a just distinction from striking, which<br>
is ever a less lasting effect, and more generally belongs to the fair<br>
complexions; but leaving that decision to every one&rsquo;s taste, I proceed<br>
to give you Louisa&rsquo;s narrative as follows:<br>
<br>
&ldquo;According to practical maxims of life, I ought to boast of my birth,<br>
since I owe it to pure love, without marriage; but this I know, it was<br>
scarce possible to inherit a stronger propensity to that cause of my<br>
being than I did. I was the rare production of the first essay of a<br>
journeyman cabinet-maker, on his master&rsquo;s maid: the consequence of<br>
which was a big belly, and the loss of a place. He was not in<br>
circumstances to do much for her; and yet, after all this blemish, she<br>
found means, after she had dropt her burthen, and disposed of me to a<br>
poor relation in the country, to repair it by marrying a pastry-cook<br>
here in London, in thriving business; on whom she soon, under favour of<br>
the complete ascendant he had given her over him, passed me for a child<br>
she had by her first husband. I had, on that footing, been taken home,<br>
and was not six years old when this father-in-law died, and left my<br>
mother in tolerable circumstances, and without any children by him. As<br>
to my natural father, he had betaken himself to the sea; where, when<br>
the truth of things came out, I was told that he died, not immensely<br>
rich you may think, since he was no more than a common sailor. As I<br>
grew up, under the eyes of my mother, who kept on the business, I could<br>
not but see, in her severe watchfulness, the marks of a slip, which she<br>
did not care should be hereditary; but we no more choose our passions<br>
than our features or complexions, and the bent of mine was so strong to<br>
the forbidden pleasure, that it got the better, at length, of all her<br>
care and precaution. I was scarce twelve years old, before that part<br>
which she wanted so much to keep out of harm&rsquo;s way, made me feel its<br>
impatience to be taken notice of, and come into play; already had it<br>
put forth the signs of forwardness in the sprout of a soft down over<br>
it, which had often fluttered, and I might also say, grown under my<br>
constant touch and visitation, so pleased was I with what I took to be<br>
a kind of title to womanhood, that state I pined to be entered of, for<br>
the pleasures I conceived were annexed to it; and now the growing<br>
importance of that part to me, and the new sensations in it, demolished<br>
at once all my girlish play-things and amusements. Nature now pointed<br>
me strongly to more solid diversions, while all the stings of desire<br>
settled so fiercely in that little centre of them, that I could not<br>
mistake the spot I wanted a playfellow in.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;I now shunned all company in which there was no hopes of coming at the<br>
object of my longings, and used to shut myself up, to indulge in<br>
solitude some tender meditation on the pleasure I strongly perceived<br>
the overture of, in feeling and examining what nature assured me must<br>
be the chosen avenue, the gates for unknown bliss to enter at, that I<br>
panted after.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;But these meditations only increased my disorder, and blew the fire<br>
that consumed me. I was yet worse when, yielding at length to the<br>
insupportable irritations of the little fairy charm that tormented me,<br>
I seized it with my fingers, teazing it to no end. Sometimes, in the<br>
furious excitations of desire, I threw myself on the bed, spread my<br>
thighs abroad, and lay as it were expecting the longed-for relief, till<br>
finding my illusion, I shut and squeezed them together again, burning<br>
and fretting. In short, this develish thing, with its impetuous girds<br>
and itching fires, led me such a life, that I could neither, night or<br>
day, be at peace with it or myself. In time, however, I thought I had<br>
gained a prodigious prize, when figuring to myself that my fingers were<br>
something of the shape of what I pined for, I worked my way in with one<br>
of them with great agitation and delight; yet not without pain too did<br>
I deflower myself as far as it could reach; proceeding with such a fury<br>
of passion, in this solitary and last shift of pleasure, as extended me<br>
at length breathless on the bed in an amorous melting trance.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;But frequency of use dulling the sensation, I soon began to perceive<br>
that this work was but a paultry shallow expedient, that went but a<br>
little way to relieve me, and rather raised more flame than its dry and<br>
insignificant titillation could rightly appease.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;Man alone, I almost instinctively knew, as well as by what I had<br>
industriously picked up at weddings and christenings, was possessed of<br>
the only remedy that could reduce this rebellious disorder; but watched<br>
and overlooked as I was, how to come at it was the point, and that, to<br>
all appearance, an invincible one; not that I did not rack my brains<br>
and invention how at once to elude my mothers vigilance, and procure<br>
myself the satisfaction of my impetuous curiosity and longings for this<br>
mighty and untasted pleasure. At length, however, a singular chance did<br>
at once the work of a long course of alertness. One day that we had<br>
dined at an acquaintance over the way, together with a<br>
gentlewoman-lodger that occupied the first floor of our house, there<br>
started an indispensable necessity for my mother&rsquo;s going down to<br>
Greenwich to accompany her: the party was settled, when I do not know<br>
what genius whispered me to plead a headache, which I certainly had<br>
not, against my being included in a jaunt that I had not the least<br>
relish for. The pretext, however, passed, and my mother, with much<br>
reluctance, prevailed with herself to go without me; but took<br>
particular care to see me safe home, where she consigned me into the<br>
hands of an old trusty maidservants, who served in the shop, for we had<br>
not a male creature in the house.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;As soon as she was gone, I told the maid I would go up and lie down on<br>
our lodger&rsquo;s bed, mine not being made, with a charge to her at the same<br>
time not to disturb me, as it was only rest I wanted. This injunction<br>
probably proved of eminent service to me. As soon as I was got into the<br>
bedchamber, I unlaced my stays, and threw myself on the outside of the<br>
bedclothes, in all the loosest undress. Here I gave myself up to the<br>
old insipid privy shifts of my self-viewing, self-touching<br>
self-enjoying, in fine, to all the means of self knowledge I could<br>
devise, in search of the pleasure that fled before me, and tantalized<br>
with that unknown something that was out of my reach; thus all only<br>
served to enflame myself, and to provoke violently my desires, whilst<br>
the one thing needful to their satisfaction was not at hand, and I<br>
could have bit my finger for representing it so ill. After then<br>
wearying and fatiguing myself with grasping shadows, whilst that most<br>
sensible part of me disdained to content itself with less than<br>
realities, the strong yearnings, the urgent struggles of nature towards<br>
the melting relief, and the extreme self-agitations I had used to come<br>
at it, had wearied and thrown me into a kind of unquiet sleep: for, if<br>
I tossed and threw about my limbs in proportion to the distraction of<br>
my dreams, as I had reason to believe I did, a bystander could not have<br>
helped seeing all for love. And one there was it seems; for waking out<br>
of my very short slumber, I found my hand locked in that of a young<br>
man, who was kneeling at my bed-side, and begging my pardon for his<br>
boldness: but that being a son to the lady to whom, this bed-chamber,<br>
he knew, belonged, he had slipped by the servant of the shop, as he<br>
supposed, unperceived, when finding me asleep, his first ideas were to<br>
withdraw; but that he had been fixed and detained there by a power he<br>
could better account for, than resist.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;What shall I say? my emotions of fear and surprise were instantly<br>
subdued by those of the pleasure I bespoke in great presence of mind<br>
from the turn this adventure might take. He seemed to me no other than<br>
a pitying angel, dropt out of the clouds: for he was young and<br>
perfectly handsome, which was more than even I had asked for, man, in<br>
general, being all that my utmost desires had pointed at. I thought<br>
then I could not put too much encouragement into my eyes and voice; I<br>
regretted no leading advances; no matter for his after-opinion of my<br>
forwardness, so it might bring him to the point of answering my<br>
pressing demands of present case; it was not now with his thoughts but<br>
his actions that my business immediately lay. I raised then my head,<br>
and told him, in a soft tone, that tended to prescribe the same key to<br>
him, that his mamma was gone out and would not return till late at<br>
night: which I thought no bad hint; but as it proved, I had nothing of<br>
a novice to deal with. The impressions I had made on him from the<br>
discoveries I had betrayed of my person in the disordered motions of<br>
it, during his view of me asleep, had, as he afterwards told me, so<br>
fixed and charmingly prepared him, that, had I known his dispositions,<br>
I had more to hope from his violence, than to fear from his respect;<br>
and even less than the extreme tenderness which I threw into my voice<br>
and eyes, would have served to encourage him to make the most of the<br>
opportunity. Finding then that his kisses, imprinted on my hand, were<br>
taken as tamely as he could wish, he rose to my lips; and glewing his<br>
to them, made me so faint with overcoming joy and pleasure, that I fell<br>
back, and he with me, in course, on the bed, upon which I had, by<br>
insensibly shifting from the side to near the middle, invitingly, made<br>
room for him. He is now lain down by me, and the minutes being too<br>
precious to consume in ultimate ceremony, or dalliance, my youth<br>
proceeds immediately to those extremities, which all my looks, humming<br>
and palpitations, had assured him he might attempt without the fear of<br>
a repulse: those rogues the men, read us admirably on these occasions.<br>
I lay then at length panting for the imminent attack, with wishes far<br>
beyond my fears, and for which it was scarce possible for a girl,<br>
barely thirteen, but tall and well grown, to have better dispositions.<br>
He threw up my petticoat and shift, whilst my thighs were, by an<br>
instinct of nature, unfolded to their best; and my desires had so<br>
thoroughly destroyed all modesty in me, that even their being now naked<br>
and all laid open to him, was part of the prelude that pleasure<br>
deepened my blushes at, more than same. But when his hand, and touches,<br>
naturally attracted to their center, made me feel all their wantonness<br>
and warmth in, and round it, oh! how immensely different a sense of<br>
things, did I perceive there, than when under my own insipid handling!<br>
And now his waistcoat was unbuttoned, and the confinement of the<br>
breeches burst through, when out started to view the amazing, pleasing<br>
object of all my wishes, all my dreams, all my love, the king member<br>
indeed! I gazed at, I devoured it, at length and breadth, with my eyes<br>
intently directed to it, till his; getting upon me, and placing between<br>
my thighs, took from me the enjoyment of its sight, to give me a far<br>
more grateful one, in its touch, in that part where its touch is so<br>
exquisitely affecting. Applying it then to the minute opening, for such<br>
at that age it certainly was, I met with too much good will, I felt<br>
with too great a rapture of pleasure the first insertion of it, to heed<br>
much the pain that followed: I thought nothing too dear to pay for this<br>
the richest treat of the sense; so that, split up, torn, bleeding,<br>
mangled I was still superiorly pleased, and hugged the author of all<br>
this delicious ruin. But when, soon after, he made his second attack,<br>
sore as every thing was, the smart was soon put away by the sovereign<br>
cordial; all my soft complainings were silenced, and the pain melting<br>
fast away into pleasure. I abandoned myself over to all its transports,<br>
and gave it the full possession of my whole body and soul; for now all<br>
thought was at an end with me; I lived in what I felt only. And who<br>
could describe those feelings, those agitations, yet exalted by the<br>
charm of their novelty and surprise? when that part of me which had so<br>
hungered for the dear morsel that now so delightfully crammed, forced<br>
all my vital sensations to fix their home there, during the stay of my<br>
beloved guest; who too soon paid me for his hearty welcome, in a<br>
dissolvent, richer far than that I have heard of some queen treating<br>
her paramour with, in liquified pearl, and ravishingly poured into me,<br>
where, now myself too much melted to give it a dry reception, I hailed<br>
it with the warmest confluence on my side, amidst all those ecstatic<br>
raptures, not unfamiliar I presume to this good company. Thus, however,<br>
I arrived at the very top of all my wishes, by an accident unexpected<br>
indeed, but not so wonderful; for this young gentleman was just arrived<br>
in town from college, and came familiarly to his mother at her<br>
apartment, where he had once before been, though, by mere chance. I had<br>
not seen him: so that we knew one another by hearing only; and finding<br>
me stretched on his mother&rsquo;s bed, he readily concluded from her<br>
description, who it was. The rest you know.<br>
<br>
&ldquo;This affair had however no ruinous consequences, the young gentleman<br>
escaping then, and many more times undiscovered. But the warmth of my<br>
constitution, that made the pleasures of love a kind of necessary of<br>
life to me, having betrayed me into indiscretions fatal to my private<br>
fortune, I fell at length to the public; from which, it is probable, I<br>
might have met with the worst of ruin, if my better fate had not thrown<br>
me into this safe and agreeable refuge.&rdquo;<br>
<br>
Here Louisa ended; and these little histories having brought the time<br>
for the girls to retire, and to prepare for the revels of the evening,<br>
I staid with Mrs. Cole, till Emily came, and told us the company was<br>
met, and waited for us.<br>
<br>
Mrs. Cole on this, taking me by the hand, with a smile of<br>
encouragement, led me up stairs, preceded by Louisa, who was come to<br>
hasten us, and lighted us with two candles, one in each hand.<br>
<br>
On the landing-place of the first pair of stairs, we were met by a<br>
young gentleman, extremely well dressed, and a very pretty figure, to<br>
whom I was to be indebted for the first essay of the pleasures of the<br>
house. He saluted me with great gallantry, and handed me into the<br>
drawing room, the floor of which was overspread with a Turkey carpet,<br>
and all its furniture voluptuously adapted to every demand of the most<br>
studied luxury; now too it was, by means of a profuse illumination,<br>
enlivened by a light scarce inferior, and perhaps more favourable to<br>
joy, more tenderly pleasing, than that of broad sunshine.<br>
<br>
On my entrance into the room, I had the satisfaction! to hear a buzz of<br>
approbation run through the whole company, which now consisted of four<br>
gentlemen, including my particular (this was the cant term of the house<br>
for one&rsquo;s gallant for the time), the three young-women, in a neat<br>
flowing dishabille, the mistress of the academy, and myself. I was<br>
welcomed and saluted by a kiss all round, in which, however, it was<br>
easy to discover, in the superior warmth of that of the men, the<br>
distinction of the sexes.<br>
<br>
Awed, and confounded as I was, at seeing myself surrounded, caressed,<br>
and made court to by so many strangers, I could not immediately<br>
familiarize myself to all that air of gaiety and joy, which dictated<br>
their compliments, and animated their caresses.<br>
<br>
They assured me that I was so perfectly to their taste, as to have but<br>
one fault against me, which I might easily be cured of, and that was my<br>
modesty: this, they observed, might pass for a beauty the more with<br>
those who wanted it for a heightener; but their maxim was, that it was<br>
an impertinent mixture, and dashed the cup so as to spoil the sincere<br>
draught of pleasure; they considered it accordingly as their mortal<br>
enemy, and gave it no quarter wherever they met with it. This was a<br>
prologue not unworthy of the revels that ensued.<br>
<br>
In the midst of all the frolic and wantonness, which this joyous band<br>
had presently, and all naturally, run into, an elegant supper was<br>
served in, and we sat down to it, my spark elect placing himself next<br>
to me, and the other couples without order or ceremony. The delicate<br>
cheer and good wine soon banished all reserve; the conversation grew as<br>
lively as could be wished, without taking too loose a turn: these<br>
professors of pleasure knew too well, how to stale impressions of it,<br>
or evaporate the imagination of words, before the time of action.<br>
Kisses however were snatched at times, or where a handkerchief round<br>
the neck interposed its feeble barrier, it was not extremely respected:<br>
the hands of the men went to work with their usual petulance, till the<br>
provocation on both sides rose to such a pitch, that my particulars&rsquo;s<br>
proposal for beginning the country dances was received with instant<br>
assent: for, as he laughingly added, he fancied the instruments were in<br>
tune. This was a signal for preparation, that the complaisant Mrs.<br>
Cole, who understood life, took for her cue of disappearing; no longer<br>
so fit for personal service herself, and content with having settled<br>
the order of battle, she left us the field, to fight it out at<br>
discretion.<br>
<br>
As soon as she was gone, the table was removed from the middle, and<br>
became a side-board; a couch was brought into its place, of which when<br>
I whisperingly inquired the reason, of my particular, he told me, &ldquo;that<br>
as it was chiefly on my account that his convention was met, the<br>
parties intended at once to humour their taste of variety in pleasures,<br>
and by an open public enjoyment, to see me broke of any taint of<br>
reserve or modesty, which they looked on as the poison of joy; that<br>
though they occasionally preached pleasure, and lived up to the text,<br>
they did not enthusiastically set up for missionaries, and only<br>
indulged themselves in the delights of a practical instruction of all<br>
the pretty women they liked well enough to bestow it upon, and who fell<br>
properly in the way of it; but that as such a proposal might be too<br>
violent, too shocking for a young beginner, the old standers were to<br>
set an example, which he hoped I would not be averse to follow, since<br>
it was to him I was devolved in favour of the first experiment; but<br>
that still I was perfectly at my liberty to refuse the party, which<br>
being in its nature one of pleasure, supposed an exclusion of all force<br>
or constraint.&rdquo;<br>
<br>
My countenance expressed, no doubt, my surprise as my silence did my<br>
acquiescence. I was now embarked, and thoroughly determined on any<br>
voyage the company would take me on.<br>
<br>
The first that stood up, to open the ball, were a cornet of horse, and<br>
that sweetest of olive-beauties, the soft and amorous Louisa. He led<br>
her to the couch (nothing loth), on which he gave her the fall, and<br>
extended her at length with an air of roughness and vigour, relishing<br>
high of amorous eagerness and impatience. The girl, spreading herself<br>
to the best advantage, with her head upon the pillow, was so<br>
concentered in that she was about, that our presence was the least of<br>
her care and concern. Her petticoats, thrown up with her shift,<br>
discovered to the company the finest turned legs and thighs that could<br>
be imagined, and in broad display, that gave us a full view of that<br>
delicious cleft of flesh, into which the pleasing hair, grown mount<br>
over it, parted and presented a most inviting entrance, between two<br>
close hedges, delicately soft and pouting. Her gallant was now ready,<br>
having disencumbered himself from his clothes, overloaded with lace,<br>
and presently, his shirt removed, shewed us his forces at high plight,<br>
bandied and ready for action. But giving us no time to consider the<br>
dimensions, he threw himself instantly over his charming antagonist who<br>
received him as he pushed at once dead at mark, like a heroine, without<br>
flinching; for surely never was girl constitutionally truer to the<br>
taste of joy, or sincerer in the expressions of its sensations, than<br>
she was: we could observe pleasure lighten in her eyes, as he<br>
introduced his plenipotentiary instrument into her; till, at length,<br>
having indulged her to its utmost reach, its irritations grew so<br>
violent, and gave her the spurs so furiously, that collected within<br>
herself, and lost to every thing but the enjoyment of her favourite<br>
feelings, she retarded his thrusts with a just concert of spring<br>
heaves, keeping time so exactly with the most pathetic sighs, that one<br>
might have numbered the strokes in agitation by their distinct murmurs,<br>
whilst her active limbs kept wreathing and intertwisting with his, in<br>
convulsive folds: then the turtle-billing kisses, and the poignant<br>
painless lovebites, which they both exchanged, in a rage of delight,<br>
all conspiring towards the melting period. It soon came on, when<br>
Louisa, in the ravings of her pleasure-frensy, impotent of all<br>
restraint, cried out: &ldquo;Oh Sir!... Good Sir! pray do not spare me! ah!<br>
ah!...&rdquo; All her accents now faultering into heart-fetched sighs, she<br>
closed her eyes in the sweet death, in the instant of which we could<br>
easily see the signs in the quiet, dying, languid posture of her late<br>
so furious driver, who was stopped of a sudden, breathing short,<br>
panting, and, for that time, giving up the spirit of pleasure. As soon<br>
as he was dismounted, Louisa sprung up, shook her petticoats, and<br>
running up to me, gave me a kiss, and drew me to the side-board, to<br>
which she was herself handed by her gallant, where they made me pledge<br>
them in a glass of wine, and toast a droll health of Louisa&rsquo;s proposal<br>
in high frolic.<br>
<br>
By this time the second couple was ready to enter the lists: which were<br>
a young baronet, and that delicatest of charmers, the winning, tender<br>
Harriet. My gentle esquire came to acquaint me with it, and brought me<br>
back to the scene of action.<br>
<br>
And, surely, never did one of her profession accompany her<br>
dispositions, for the barefaced part she was engaged to play, with such<br>
a peculiar grace of sweetness, modesty and yielding coyness, as she<br>
did. All her air and motions breathed only unreserved, unlimited<br>
complaisance without the least mixture of impudence, or prostitution.<br>
But what was yet more surprising, her spark elect, in the midst of the<br>
dissolution of a public open enjoyment, doated on her to distraction,<br>
and had, by dint of love and sentiments, touched her heart, though for<br>
a while the restraint of their engagement to the house laid him under a<br>
kind of necessity of complying with an institution which himself had<br>
had the greatest share establishing.<br>
<br>
Harriet was then led to the vacant couch by her gallant, blushing as<br>
she looked at me, and with eyes made to justify any thing, tenderly<br>
bespeaking of me the most favourable construction of the step she was<br>
thus irresistibly drawn into.<br>
<br>
Her lover, for such he was, sat her down at the foot of the couch, and<br>
passing his arm round her neck, preluded with a kiss fervently applied<br>
to her lips, that visibly gave her life and spirit to go through with<br>
the scene; and as he kissed, he gently inclined her head, till it fell<br>
back on a pillow disposed to receive it, and leaning himself down all<br>
the way with her, at once countenanced and endeared her fall to her.<br>
There, as if he had guessed our wishes, or meant to gratify at once his<br>
pleasure and his pride, in being the master, by the title of present<br>
possession, of beauties delicate beyond imagination, he discovered her<br>
breast to his own touch, and our common view; but oh! what delicious<br>
manual of love devotion; how inimitable fine moulded! small, round,<br>
firm, and excellently white; then the grain of their skin, so soothing,<br>

suspicion, was taken away; and this was not the work of the fourth part<br>
of a minute, and of which ever side one lay, the thing was equally easy<br>
and practicable, by the double care taken to have each bed-post<br>
provided alike. True it is, that had he waked and caught me in the act,<br>
it would at least have covered me with shame and confusion; but them,<br>
that he did not, was, with the precautions I took, a risk of a thousand<br>
to one in my favour.<br>
<br>
At ease now, and out of all fear of any doubt or suspicion on his side,<br>
I addressed myself in good earnest to my repose, but could obtain none;<br>
and in about half an hour&rsquo;s time my gentleman waked again, and turning<br>
towards me, I feigned a sound sleep, which he did not long respect; but<br>
girding himself again to renew the onset, he began to kiss and caress<br>
me, when now making as if I just waked, I complained of the<br>
disturbance, and of the cruel pain that this little rest had stole my<br>
senses from. Eager, however, for the pleasure, as well of consummating<br>
an entire triumph over my virginity, he said every thing that could<br>
overcome my resistance, and bribe my patience to the end, which now I<br>
was ready to listen to, from being secure of the bloody proofs I had<br>
prepared of his victorious violence, though I still thought it good<br>
policy not to let him in yet a while. I answered then only to his<br>
importunities in sighs and moans, &ldquo;that I was so hurt, I could not bear<br>
it... I was sure he had done me a mischief; that he had... he was such<br>
a bad man!&rdquo; At this, turning down the clothes, and viewing the field of<br>
battle by the glimmer of a dying taper, he saw plainly my thighs,<br>
shift, and sheet, all stained with what he readily took for a virgin<br>
effusion, proceeding from his last half penetration: convinced, and<br>
transported at which, nothing could equal his joy and exultation. The<br>
illusion was complete, no other conception entered his head, but that<br>
of his having been at work upon an unopened mine; which idea, upon so<br>
strong an evidence, redoubled at once his tenderness for me, and his<br>
ardour for breaking it wholly up. Kissing me then with the utmost<br>
rapture, he comforted me, and begged my pardon for the pain he had put<br>
me to: observing withal, that it was only a thing in course; but the<br>
worst was certainly past, and that with a little courage and constancy,<br>
I should get it once well over, and never after experience any thing<br>
but the greatest pleasure. By little and little I suffered myself to be<br>
prevailed on, and giving, as it were, up to the point of him, I made my<br>
thighs, insensibly spreading them, yield him liberty of access, which<br>
improving, he got a little within me, when by a well managed reception<br>
I worked the female screw so nicely, that I kept him from the easy<br>
mid-channel direction, and by dexterous wreathing and contortions,<br>
creating an artificial difficulty of entrance, made him win it inch by<br>
inch, with the most laborious struggles, I all the while sorely<br>
complaining: till at length, with might and main, winding his way in,<br>
he got it completely home, and giving my virginity, as he thought, the<br>
coup le grace, furnished me with the cue of setting up a terrible<br>
outcry, whilst he, triumphant and like a cock clapping his wings over<br>
his down-trod mistress, pursued his pleasure: which presently rose, in<br>
virtue of this idea of a complete victory, to a pitch that made me soon<br>
sensible of his melting period; whilst I now lay acting the deep<br>
wounded, breathless, frightened, undone, no longer maid.<br>
<br>
You would ask me, perhaps, whether all this time I enjoyed any<br>
perception of pleasure? I assure you, little or none, till just towards<br>
the latter end, a faintish sense of it came on mechanically, from so<br>
long a struggle and frequent fret in that ever sensible part; but, in<br>
the first place, I had no taste for the person I was suffering the<br>
embraces of, on a pure mercenary account; and then, I was not entirely<br>
delighted with myself for the jade&rsquo;s part I was playing, whatever<br>
excuses I might plead for my being brought into it; but then this<br>
insensibility kept me so much the mistress of my mind and motions, that<br>
I could the better manage so close a counterfeit, through the whole<br>
scene of deception.<br>
<br>
Recovered at length to a more shew of life, by his tender condolences,<br>
kisses and embraces, I upbraided him, and reproached him with my ruin,<br>
in such natural terms, as added to his satisfaction with himself, for<br>
having accomplished it; and guessing, by certain observations of mine,<br>
that it would be rather favourable to him, to spare him, when he some<br>
time after, feebly enough, came on again to the assault, I resolutely<br>
withstood any further endeavours, on a pretext that flattered his<br>
prowess, of my being so violently hurt and sore, that I could not<br>
possibly endure a fresh trial. He then graciously granted me a respite,<br>
and the next morning soon after advancing, I got rid of further<br>
importunity, till Mrs. Cole, being rung for by him, came in and was<br>
made acquainted, in terms of the utmost joy and rapture, with his<br>
triumphant certainty of my virtue, and the finishing stroke he had<br>
given it, in the course of the night: of which, he added, she would see<br>
proof enough in bloody characters, on the sheets.<br>
<br>
You may guess how a woman of her turn of address and experience<br>
humoured the jest, and played him off with mixed exclamations of shame,<br>
danger, compassion for me, and of her being pleased that all was so<br>
well over: in which last, I believe, she was certainly sincere. And<br>
now, as the objection which she had represented as an invincible one,<br>
to me lying the first night at his lodgings (which were studiously<br>
calculated for freedom of intrigues), on the account of my maiden fears<br>
and terrors, at the thought of going to a gentleman&rsquo;s chambers, and<br>
being alone with him in bed, was surmounted, she pretended to persuade<br>
me, in favour to him, that I should go there to him, whenever he<br>
pleased, and still keep up all the necessary appearances of working<br>
with her, that I might not lose, with my character, the prospect of<br>
getting a good husband, and at the same time her house would be kept<br>
safer from scandal. All this seemed so reasonable, so considerate to<br>
Mr. Norbert, that he never once perceived that she did not want him to<br>
resort to her house, lest he might in time discover certain<br>
inconsistencies with the character she had set out with to him: besides<br>
that this plan greatly flattered his own ease, and views of liberty.<br>
<br>
Leaving me then to my much wanted rest, he got up, and Mrs. Cole, after<br>
settling with him all points relating to me, got him undiscovered out<br>
of the house. After which, as I was awake, she came in, and gave me due<br>
praises for my success. Behaving too with her usual moderation and<br>
disinterestedness, she refused any share of the sum I had thus earned,<br>
and put me into such a secure and easy way of disposing of my affairs,<br>
which now amounted to a kind of little fortune, that a child of ten<br>
years old might have kept the account and property of them safe in its<br>
hands.<br>
<br>
I was now restored again to my former state of a kept mistress, and<br>
used punctually to wait on Mr. Norbert at his chambers whenever he sent<br>
a messenger for me, which I constantly took care to be in the way of,<br>
and managed with so much caution, that he never once penetrated the<br>
nature of my connections with Mrs. Cole; but indolently given up to<br>
ease and the town dissipations, the perpetual hurry of them hindered<br>
him from looking into his own affairs, much less to mine.<br>
<br>
In the mean time, if I may judge from my own experience, none are<br>
better paid, or better treated, during their reign, than the mistress<br>
of those who, enervate by nature, debaucheries, or age, have the least<br>
employment for the sex: sensible that a woman must be satisfied some<br>
way, they ply her with a thousand little tender attentions, presents,<br>
caresses, confidences, and exhaust their inventions in means and<br>
devices to make up for the capital deficiency; and even towards<br>
lessening that, what arts, what modes, what refinements of pleasure<br>
have they not recourse to, to raise their languid powers, and press<br>
nature into the service of their sensuality? But here is their<br>
misfortune, that when by a course of teasing, worrying, handling,<br>
wanton postures, lascivious motions, they have at length accomplished a<br>
flashy enervate enjoyment, they at the same time light up a flame in<br>
the object of their passion, that, not having the means themselves to<br>
quench, drives her for relief into the next person&rsquo;s arms, who can<br>
finish their work; and thus they become bawds to some favourite, tried<br>
and approved of, for a more vigorous and satisfactory execution; for<br>
with women, of our turn especially, however well our hearts may be<br>
disposed, there is a controlling part, or queen-seat in us, that<br>
governs itself by its own maxims of state, amongst which not one is<br>
stronger, in practice with it, than, in the matter of is dues, never to<br>
accept the will for the deed.<br>
<br>
Mr. Norbert, who was much in this ungracious case, though he professed<br>
to like me extremely, could but seldom consummate the main-joy itself<br>
with me, without such a length and variety of preparations, as were at<br>
once wearisome and inflammatory.<br>
<br>
Sometimes he would strip me stark naked on a carpet, by a good fire,<br>
when he would contemplate me almost by the hour, disposing me in all<br>
the figures and attitudes of body that it was susceptible of being<br>
viewed in; kissing me in every part, the most secret and critical one<br>
so far from excepted that it received most of that branch of homage.<br>
Then his touches were so exquisitely wanton, so luxuriously diffused<br>
and penetrative at times, that he had made me perfectly rage with<br>
titillating fires, when, after all, and much ado, he had gained a<br>
short-lived erection, he would perhaps melt it away in a washy sweat,<br>
or a premature abortive effusion, that provokingly mocked my eager<br>
desires: or, if carried home, how faultered and unnervous the<br>
execution! how insufficient the sprinkle of a few heat-drops to<br>
extinguish all the flames he had kindled!<br>
<br>
One evening, I cannot help remembering, that returning home from him,<br>
with a spirit he had raised in a circle his wand had proved too weak to<br>
lay, as I turned the corner of a street, I was overtaken by a young<br>
sailor, I was then in that spruce, neat, plain dress, which I ever<br>
affected and perhaps might have, in my trip, a certain air of<br>
restlessness unknown to the composure of cooler thoughts. However, he<br>
seized me as a prize, and without farther ceremony threw his arms round<br>
my neck, and kissed me boisterously and sweetly. I looked at him with a<br>
beginning of anger and indignation at his rudeness, that softened away<br>
into other sentiments as I viewed him: for he was tall, manly<br>
carriaged, handsome of body and face, so that I ended my stare, with<br>
asking him, in a tone turned to tenderness, what he meant; at which,<br>
with the same frankness and vivacity as he had begun with me, he<br>
proposed treating me with a glass of wine. Now, certain it is, that had<br>
I been in a calmer state of blood than I was, had I not been under the<br>
dominion of unappeased irritation; but I do not know how it was, my<br>
pressing calls, his figure, the occasion, and if you will, the powerful<br>
combination of all these, with a start of curiosity to see the end of<br>
an adventure, so novel too as being treated like a common street-plyer,<br>
made me give a silent consent; in short, it was not my head that I now<br>
obeyed, I suffered myself to be towed along as it were by this<br>
man-of-war, who took me under his arm as familialry as if he had known<br>
me all his lifetime, and led me into the next convenient tavern, where<br>
we were shown into a little room on one side of the passage. Here,<br>
scarce allowing himself patient till the drawer brought in the wine<br>
called for, he fell directly on board me: when, untucking my<br>
handkerchief, and giving me a snatching buss, he laid my breasts bare<br>
at once, which he handled with that keenness of gust that abridges a<br>
ceremonial evermore tiresome than pleasing on such pressing occasions;<br>
and now, hurrying towards the main point, we found no conveniency to<br>
our purpose, two or three disabled chairs, and a rickety table,<br>
composing the whole furniture of the room. Without more ado, he plans<br>
me with my back standing against the wall, and my petticoats up; and<br>
coming out with a splitter indeed, made it shine, as he brandished it,<br>
in my eyes; and going to work with an impetuosity and eagerness, bred<br>
very likely by a long fast at seat, went to give me a taste of it. I<br>
straddled, I humoured my posture, and did my best in short to buckle to<br>
it; I took part of it in, but still things did not go to his thorough<br>
liking; changing them in a trice his system of battery, he leads me to<br>
the table and with a master-hand lays my head down on the edge of it,<br>
and, with the other canting up my petticoats and shift, bares my naked<br>
posteriors to his blind and furious guide; it forces its way between<br>
them, and I feeling pretty sensibly that it was not going by the right<br>
door, and knocking desperately at the wrong one, I told him of<br>
it:&mdash;&ldquo;Pooh!&rdquo; says he, &ldquo;my dear, any port in a storm.&rdquo; Altering, however,<br>
directly his course, and lowering his point, he fixed it right, and<br>
driving it up with a delicious stiffness, made all foam again, and gave<br>
me the tout with such fire and spirit, that in the fine disposition I<br>
was in when I submitted to him and stirred up so fiercely as I was, I<br>
got the start of him, and went away into the melting swoon, and<br>
squeezing him, whilst in the convulsive grasp of it, drew from him such<br>
a plenteous bedewal, as pointed to my own effusion, perfectly floated<br>
those parts, and drowned in a deluge all my raging conflagration of<br>
desire.<br>
<br>
When this was over, how to make my retreat was my concern; for, though<br>
I had been so extremely pleased with the difficult between this warm<br>
broadside, poured so briskly into me, and the tiresome pawing and<br>
toying to which I had owed the unappeased flames that had driven me<br>
into this step, now I was cooler, I began to apprehend the danger of<br>
contracting an acquaintance with this, however agreeable stranger; who,<br>
on his side, spoke of passing the evening with me and continuing our<br>
intimacy, with an air of determination that made me afraid of its being<br>
not so easy to get away from him as I could wish. In the mean time I<br>
carefully concealed my uneasiness, and readily pretended to consent to<br>
stay with him, telling him I should only step to my lodgings to leave a<br>
necessary direction, and then instantly return. This he very glibly<br>
swallowed, on the notion of my being one of those unhappy<br>
street-errants, who devote themselves to the pleasure of the first<br>
ruffian that will stoop to pick them up, and of course, that I would<br>
scarce bilk myself of the hire, by not returning make the most of the<br>
job. Thus he parted with me, not before, however, he had ordered in my<br>
hearing a supper, which I had the barbarity to disappoint him of my<br>
company too.<br>
<br>
But when I got home, and told Mrs. Cole my adventure, she represented<br>
so strongly to me the nature and dangerous consequences of my folly,<br>
particularly the risks to my health, in being so openlegged and free,<br>
that I not only took resolutions never to venture so rashly again,<br>
which I inviolably preserved, but passed a good many days in continual<br>
uneasiness, lest I should have met with other reasons, besides the<br>
pleasure of that rencounter, to remember it; but these fears wronged my<br>
pretty sailor, for which I gladly make him this reparation.<br>
<br>
I had now lived with Mr. Norbert near a quarter of a year, in which<br>
space I circulated my time very pleasantly, between my amusements at<br>
Mrs. Cole&rsquo;s, and a proper attendance on that gentleman, who paid me<br>
profusely for the unlimited complaisance with which I passively<br>
humoured every caprice of pleasure, and which had won upon him so<br>
greatly, that finding, as he said, all that variety in me alone, which<br>
he had sought for in a number of women, I had made him lose his taste<br>
for inconstancy, and new faces. But what was yet at least agreeable, as<br>
well as more flattering, the love I had inspired him with, bred a<br>
deference to me, that was of great service to his health: for having by<br>
degrees, and with much pathetic representations brought him to some<br>
husbandry of it, and to insure the duration of his pleasures by<br>
moderating their use, and correcting those excesses in them he was so<br>
addicted to, and which had shattered his constitution and destroyed his<br>
powers of life in the very point for which he seemed desirous to live,<br>
he was grown more delicate, more temperate, and in course more healthy;<br>
his gratitude for which was taking a turn very favourable for my<br>
fortune, when once more the caprice of it dashed the cup from my lips.<br>
<br>
His sister, lady L..., for whom he had a great affection, desiring him<br>
to accompany her down to Bath for her health, he could not refuse her<br>
such a favour; and accordingly, though he counted on staying away from<br>
me no more than a week at farthest, he took his leave of me with an<br>
ominous heaviness of heart, and left me a sum far above the state of<br>
his fortune, and very inconsistent with the intended shortness of his<br>
journey; but it ended in the longest that can be, and is never but once<br>
taken: for, arrived at Bath, he was not there two days before he fell<br>
into a debauch of drinking with some gentlemen, that threw him into a<br>
high fever, and carried him off in four days&rsquo; time, never once out of a<br>
delirium. Had he been in his senses to make a will, perhaps he might<br>
have made favourable mention of me in it. Thus, however, I lost him;<br>
and as no condition of life is more subject to revolutions than that of<br>
a woman of pleasure, I soon recovered my cheerfulness, and now beheld<br>
myself once more struck off the list of kept mistresses, and returned<br>
into the bosom of the community, from which I had been in some manner<br>
taken.<br>
<br>
Mrs. Cole still continued her friendship, and offered me her assistance<br>
and advice towards another choice; but I was now in ease and affluence<br>
enough to look about me at leisure; and as to any constitutional calls<br>
of pleasure, their pressure, or sensibility, was greatly lessened by a<br>
consciousness of the ease with which they were to be satisfied at Mrs.<br>
Cole&rsquo;s house, where Louisa and Emily still continued in the old way;<br>
and my great favourite Harriet used often to come and see me, and<br>
entertain me, with her head and heart full of the happiness she enjoyed<br>
with her dear baronet, whom she loved with a tenderness and constancy,<br>
even though he was her keeper, and what is yet more, had made her<br>
independent, by a handsome provision for her and hers. I was then in<br>
this vacancy from any regular employ of my person in my way of<br>
business, when one day, Mrs. Cole, in the course of the constant<br>
confidence we lived in, acquainted me that there was one Mr. Barville,<br>
who used her house, just come to town, whom she was not a little<br>
perplexed about providing a suitable companion for; which was indeed a<br>
point of difficulty, as he was under the tyranny of a cruel taste: that<br>
of an ardent desire, not only of being unmercifully whipped himself,<br>
but of whipping others, in such sort, that though he paid extravagantly<br>
those who had the courage and complaisance to submit to his humour,<br>
there were few, delicate as he was in the choice of his subjects, who<br>
would exchange turns with him so terribly at the expense of their skin.<br>
But, what yet increased the oddity of this strange fancy was the<br>
gentleman being young; whereas it generally attacks, it seems, such as<br>
are, through age, obliged to have recourse to this experiment, for<br>
quickening the circulation of their sluggish juices, and determining a<br>
conflux of the spirits of pleasure towards those flagging shrivelly<br>
parts, that rise to life only by virtue of those titillating ardours<br>
created by the discipline of their opposites, with which they have so<br>
surprising a consent.<br>
<br>
This Mrs. Cole could not well acquaint me with, in any expectation of<br>
my offering for service: for, sufficiently easy as I was in my<br>
circumstances, it must have been the temptation of an immense interest<br>
indeed, that could have induced me to embrace such a job, neither had I<br>
ever expressed, nor indeed, felt the least impulse or curiosity to know<br>
more of a taste, that promised so much more pain than pleasure to those<br>
that stood in no need of such violent goads: what then should move me<br>
to subscribe myself voluntarily to a party of pain, foreknowing it<br>
such? Why, to tell the plain truth, it was a sudden caprice, a gust of<br>
fancy for trying a new experiment, mixed with the vanity of approving<br>
my personal courage to Mrs. Cole, that determined me, at all risks, to<br>
propose myself to her and relieve her from any further look-out.<br>
Accordingly, I at once pleased and surprised her, with a frank and<br>
unreserved tender of my person to her and her friend&rsquo;s absolute<br>
disposal on this occasion.<br>
<br>
My good temporal mother was, however, so kind as to use all the<br>
arguments she could imagine to dissuade me: but, as I found they only<br>
turned on a motive of tenderness to me, I persisted in my resolution,<br>
and thereby acquitted my offer of any suspicion of its not having been<br>
sincerely made, or out of compliment only. Acquiescing then thankfully<br>
in it, Mrs. Cole assured me &ldquo;that bating the pain I should be put to,<br>
she had no scruple to engage me to this party, which she assured me I<br>
should be liberally paid for, and which, the secrecy of the transaction<br>
preserved safe from the ridicule that otherwise vulgarly attended it;<br>
that for her part, she considered pleasure, of one sort or other, as<br>
the universal port of destination, and every wind that blew thither a<br>
good one, provided it blew nobody any harm; that she rather<br>
compassionated, than blamed those unhappy persons, who are under a<br>
subjection they cannot shake off, to those arbitrary tastes that rule<br>
their appetites of pleasures with an unaccountable control: tastes too,<br>
as infinitely diversified, as superior to, and independent of all<br>
reasoning as the different relishes or palates of mankind in their<br>
viands, some delicate stomach nauseating plain meats, and finding no<br>
savour but in highseasoned, luxurious dishes, whilst others again pique<br>
themselves upon detesting them.&rdquo;<br>
<br>
I stood now in no need of this preamble of encouragement, or<br>
justification: my word was given, and I was determined to fulfill my<br>
engagements. Accordingly the night was set, and I had all the necessary<br>
previous instructions how to act and conduct myself. The dining room<br>
was duly prepared and lighted up, and the young gentleman posted there<br>
in waiting, for my introduction to him.<br>
<br>
I was then, by Mrs. Cole, brought in, and presented to him, in a loose<br>
dishabille fitted, by her direction, to the exercise I was to go<br>
through, all in the finest linen and a thorough white uniform: gown,<br>
petticoat, stocking, and satin slippers, like a victim led to<br>
sacrifice; whilst my dark auburn hair, falling in drop-curls over my<br>
neck, created a pleasing distinction of colour from the rest of my<br>
dress.<br>
<br>
As soon as Mr. Barville saw me, he got up, with a visible air of<br>
pleasure and surprise, and saluting me, asked Mrs. Cole, if so fine and<br>
delicate a creature would voluntarily submit to such sufferings and<br>
rigours, as were the subject of his assignation. She answered him<br>
properly, and now, reading in his eyes that she could not too soon<br>
leave us together, she went out, after recommending to him to use<br>
moderation with so tender a novice.<br>
<br>
But whilst she was employing his attention, mine had been taken up with<br>
examining the figure and person of this unhappy young gentleman, who<br>
was thus unaccountably condemned to have his pleasure lashed into him,<br>
as boys have their learning.<br>
<br>
He was exceedingly fair, and, smooth complexioned, and appeared to me<br>
no more than twenty at most, though he was three years older than what<br>
my conjectures gave him; but then he owed this favourable mistake to a<br>
habit of fatness, which spread through a short, squab stature; and a<br>
round, plump, fresh coloured face gave him greatly the look of a<br>
Bacchus, had not an air of austerity, not to say sternness, very<br>
unsuitable even to his shape of face, dashed that character of joy,<br>
necessary to complete the resemblance. His dress was extremely neat,<br>
but plain, and far inferior to the ample fortune he was in full<br>
possession of; this too was a taste in him, and not avarice.<br>
<br>
As soon as Mrs. Cole was gone, he seated me near him, when now his face<br>
changed upon me, into an expression of the most pleasing sweetness and<br>
good humour, the most remarkable for its sudden shift from the other<br>
extreme, which I found afterwards, when I knew more of his character,<br>
was owing to a habitual state of conflict with, and dislike of himself,<br>
for being enslaved to so peculiar a lust, by the fatality of a<br>
constitutional ascendant, that rendered him incapable of receiving any<br>
pleasure, till he submitted to these extraordinary means of procuring<br>
it at the hands of pain, whilst the constancy of this repining<br>
consciousness stamped at length that cast of sourness and severity on<br>
his features: which was, in fact, very foreign to the natural sweetness<br>
of his temper.<br>
<br>
After a competent preparation by apologies, and encouragement to go<br>
through my part with spirit and constancy, he stood up near the fire,<br>
whilst I went to fetch the instruments of discipline out of a closet<br>
hard by: these were several rods, made each of two or three strong<br>
twigs of birch tied together, which he took, handled, and viewed with<br>
as much pleasure, as I did with a kind of shuddering presage.<br>
<br>
Next we took from the side of the room a long broad bench, made easy to<br>
lie at length on by a soft cushion in a callico-cover; and everything<br>
being now ready, he took his coat and waistcoat off; and at his motion<br>
and desire, I unbuttoned his breeches, and rolling up his shirt rather<br>
above his waist, tucked it on securely there; when directing naturally<br>
my eyes to that humoursone master-movement, in whose favour all these<br>
dispositions were making, it seemed almost shrunk into his body, scarce<br>
showing its tip above the sprout of hairy curls that clothed those<br>
parts, as you may have-seen a wren peeping its head out of the grass.<br>
<br>
Stooping them to untie his garters, he gave them to me for the use of<br>
tying him down to the legs of the bench: a circumstance no farther<br>
necessary than, as I suppose, it made part of the humour of the thing,<br>
since he prescribed it to himself, amongst the rest of the ceremonial.<br>
<br>
I led him then to the bench, and according to my cue, played at forcing<br>
him to lie down: which, after-some little show of reluctance, for<br>
form-sake, he submitted to; he was straightway extended flat upon his:<br>
belly, on the bench, with a pillow under his face; and as he thus<br>
tamely lay, I tied him slightly hand and feet, to the legs of it; which<br>
done, his shirt remaining trussed up over the small of his back, I drew<br>
his breeches quite down to his knees; and now he lay, in all the<br>
fairest, broadest display of that part of the back-view; in which a<br>
pair of chubby, smooth-cheeked and passing white posteriors rose<br>
cushioning upwards from two stout, fleshful thighs, and ending their<br>
cleft, or separation by an union at the small of the back, presented a<br>
bold mark, that swelled, as it were, to meet the scourge.<br>
<br>
Seizing now one of the rods, I stood over him, and according to his<br>
direction, gave him in one breath, ten lashes with much good-will, and<br>
the utmost nerve and vigour of arm that I could put to them, so as to<br>
make those fleshy orbs quiver again under them; whilst he himself<br>
seemed no more concerned, or to mind them, than a lobster would a<br>
flea-bite. In the mean time, I view intently the effect of them, which<br>
to me at last appeared surprisingly cruel: every lash had skimmed the<br>
surface of those white cliffs, which they deeply reddened, and lapping<br>
round the side of the furthermost from me, cut specially, into the<br>
dimple of it, such livid weals, as the blood either spun out from, or<br>
stood in large drops on; and, from some of the cuts, I picked out even<br>
the splinters of the rod that had stuck in the skin. Nor was this raw<br>
work to be wondered at, considering the greenness of the twigs and the<br>
severity of the infliction, whilst the whole surface of the skin was so<br>
smooth-stretched over the hard and firm pulp of flesh that filled it,<br>
as to yield no play, or elusive swagging under the stroke: which<br>
thereby took place the more plump, and cut into the quick.<br>
<br>
I was however already so moved at the piteous sight, that I from my<br>
heart repented the undertaking, and would willing had given over,<br>
thinking he had full enough; but, he encouraging and beseeching me<br>
earnestly to proceed, I gave him ten more lashes; and then resting,<br>
surveyed the increase of bloody appearances. And at length, steeled to<br>
the height, by his stoutness in suffering, I continued the discipline,<br>
by intervals, till I observed him wreathing and twisting his body, in a<br>
way that I could plainly perceive was not the effect of pain, but of<br>
some new and powerful sensation: curious to dive into the meaning of<br>
which, in one of my pauses of intermission, I approached, as he still<br>
kept working, and grinding his belly against the cushion under him: and<br>
first stroking the untouched and unhurt side of the flesh-mount next<br>
me, then softly insinuating my hand under his thigh, felt the posture<br>
things were in forwards, which was indeed surprising: for that machine<br>
of him, which I had, by its appearance, taken for an impalpable, or at<br>
least a very diminutive subject, was now, in virtue of all that smart<br>
and havoc of his skin behind, grown not only to a prodigious stiffness<br>
of erection, but to a size that frighted even me: a non-pareil<br>
thickness indeed! the head of it alone filled the utmost capacity of my<br>
grasp. And when, as he heaved and wriggled to and fro, in the agitation<br>
of his strange pleasure, it came into view, it had something of the air<br>
of a round fillet of veal, and like its owner, squab, and short in<br>
proportion to its breadth; but when he felt my hand there, he begged I<br>
would go on briskly with my jerking, or he should never arrive at the<br>
last stage of pleasure.<br>
<br>
Resuming then the rode and the exercise of it, I had fairly worn out<br>
three bundles, when, after an increase of struggles and motion, and a<br>
deep sigh or two, I saw him lie still and motionless; and now he<br>
desired me to desist, which I instantly did; and proceeding to untie<br>
him, I could not but be amazed at his passive fortitude, on viewing the<br>
skin of his butchered, mangled posteriors, late so white, smooth and<br>
polished, now all one side of them a confused cut-work of weals, livid<br>
flesh, gashes and gore, insomuch that when he stood up, he could scarce<br>
walk; in short, he was in sweet-briars.<br>
<br>
Then I plainly perceived, on the cushion, the marks of a plenteous<br>
effusion, and already had his sluggard member run up to its old<br>
nestling-place, and enforced itself again, as if ashamed to shew its<br>
head; which nothing, it seems, could raise but stripes inflicted on its<br>
opposite neighbours, who were thus constantly obliged to suffer for his<br>
caprice.<br>
<br>
My gentleman had now put on his clothes and recomposed himself, when<br>
giving me a kiss, and placing me by him, he sat himself down as<br>
gingerly as possible, with one side off the cushion, which was too sore<br>
for him to bear resting any part of his weight on.<br>
<br>
Here he thanked me for the extreme pleasure I had procured him, and<br>
seeing, perhaps, some marks in my countenance of terror and<br>
apprehension of retaliation on my own skin, for what I had been the<br>
instrument of his suffering in his, he assured me, &ldquo;he was ready to<br>
give up to me any engagement I might deem myself under to stand him, as<br>
he had done me, but that if I proceeding in my consent to it, he would<br>
consider the difference of my sex, its greater delicacy and incapacity<br>
to undergo pain.&rdquo; Reheartened at which, and piqued in honour, as I<br>
thought, not to flinch so near the trial, especially as I well knew<br>
Mrs. Cole was an eye-witness, from her stand of espial, to the whole of<br>
our transaction, I was now less afraid of my skin, than of his not<br>
furnishing me with an opportunity of signalizing my resolution.<br>
<br>
Consonant to this disposition was my answer, but my courage was still<br>
more in my head, than in my heart; and as cowards rush into danger they<br>
fear, in order to be the sooner rid of the pain of that sensation, I<br>
was entirely pleased with his hastening matters into execution.<br>
<br>
He had then little to do, but to unloose the strings of my petticoats,<br>
and lift them, together with my shift, navel-high, where he just tucked<br>
them up loosely, and might be slipt up higher at pleasure. Then viewing<br>
me round with great seeming delight, he laid me at length on my face<br>
upon the bench, and when I expected he would tie me, as I had done him,<br>
and held out my hands, not without fear and a little trembling, he told<br>
me, &ldquo;he would by no means terrify me unnecessarily with such a<br>
confinement; for that though he meant to put my constancy to a trial,<br>
the standing it was to be completely voluntary on my side, and<br>
therefore I might be at full liberty to get up whenever I found the<br>
pain too much for me.&rdquo; You cannot imagine how much I thought myself<br>
bound, by being thus allowed to remain loose, and how much spirit this<br>
confidence in me gave me, so that I was even from my heart careless how<br>
much my flesh might suffer in honour of it.<br>
<br>
All my back parts, naked half way up, were now fully at his mercy: and<br>
first, he stood at a convenient distance, delighting himself with a<br>
gloating survey of the attitude I lay in, and of all the secret stores<br>
I thus exposed to him in fair display. Then, springing eagerly towards<br>
me, he covered all those naked parts with a fond profusion of kisses;<br>
and now, taking hold of the rod, rather wantoned with me, in gentle<br>
inflictions on those tender trembling masses of my flesh behind, than<br>
in any way hurt them, till by degrees, he began to tingle them with<br>
smarter lashes, so as to provoke a red colour into them, which I knew,<br>
as well by the flagrant glow I felt there, as by his telling me, they<br>
now emulated the native roses of my other cheeks. When he had thus<br>
amused himself with admiring, and toying with them, he went on to<br>
strike harder, and more hard, so that I needed all my patience not to<br>
cry out, or complain at least. At last, he twigged me so smartly as to<br>
fetch blood in more than one lash: at sight of which he flung down the<br>
rod, flew to me, kissed away the starting drops, and sucking the wounds<br>
eased a good deal of my pain. But now raising me on my knees, and<br>
making me kneel with them straddling wide, that tender part of me,<br>
naturally the province of pleasure, not of pain, came in for its share<br>
of suffering: for now, eyeing it wistfully, he directed the rod so that<br>
the sharp ends of the twigs lighted there, so sensibly, that I could<br>
not help wincing, and writhing my limbs with smart; so that my<br>
contortions of body must necessarily throw it into infinite variety of<br>
postures and points of view, fit to feast the luxury of the eye. But<br>
still I bore every thing without crying out: when presently giving me<br>
another pause, he rushed, as it were, on that part whose lips, and<br>
round about, had felt this cruelty, and by way of reparation, glued his<br>
own to them; then he opened, shut, squeezed them, plucked softly the<br>
overgrowing moss, and all this in a style of wild passionate rapture<br>
and enthusiasm, that expressed excess of pleasure; till betaking<br>
himself to the rod again, encouraged by my passiveness, and infuriated<br>
with this strange taste of delight, he made my poor posteriors pay for<br>
the ungovernableness of it; for now showing them no quarter, the<br>
traitor cut me so, that I wanted but little of fainting away, when he<br>
gave over. And yet I did not utter one groan, or angry expostulation;<br>
but in my heart I resolved nothing so seriously, as never to expose<br>
myself again to the like severities.<br>
<br>
You may guess then in what a curious pickle those soft flesh-cushions<br>
of mine were, all so red, raw, and in fine, terribly clawed off; but so<br>
far from feeling any pleasure in it, that the recent smart made me pout<br>
a little, and not with the greatest air of satisfaction receive the<br>
compliments, and after-caresses of the author of my pain.<br>
<br>
As soon as my clothes were huddled on in a little decency, a supper was<br>
brought in by the discreet Mrs. Cole herself, which might have piqued<br>
the sensuality of a cardinal, accompanied with a choice of the richest<br>
wines: all which she set before us, and went out again, without having,<br>
by a word or even by a smile, given us the least interruption or<br>
confusion, in those moments of secrecy, that we were not yet ripe to<br>
the admission of a third too.<br>
<br>
I sat down then, still scarce in charity with my butcher, for such I<br>
could not help considering him, and was moreover not a little piqued at<br>
the gay, satisfied air of his countenance, which I thought myself<br>
insulted by. But when the now necessary refreshment to me of a glass of<br>
wine, and a little eating (all the time observing a profound silence)<br>
had somewhat cheered and restored me to spirits, and as the smart began<br>
to go off, my good humour returned accordingly: which alteration not<br>
escaping him, he said and did every thing that could confirm me in, and<br>
indeed exalt it.<br>
<br>
But scarce was supper well over, before a change so incredible was<br>
wrought in me, such violent, yet pleasingly irksome sensations took<br>
possession of me that I scarce knew how to contain myself; the smart of<br>
the lashes was now converted into such a prickly heat, such fiery<br>
tinglings, as made me sigh, squeeze my thighs together, shift and<br>
wriggle about my seat, with a furious restlessness; whilst these<br>
itching ardours, thus excited in those parts on which the storm of<br>
discipline had principally fallen, detached legions of burning,<br>
subtile, stimulating spirits, to their opposite spot and centre of<br>
assemblage, where their titillation raged so furiously, that I was even<br>
stinging made with them. No wonder then that in such a taking, and<br>
devoured by flames that licked up all modesty and reserve, my eyes, now<br>
charged brimful of the most intense desire, fired on my companion very<br>
intelligible signal of distress: my companion, I say, who grew in them<br>
every instant more amiable, and more necessary to my urgent wishes and<br>
hopes of immediate ease.<br>
<br>
Mr. Barville, no stranger, by experience, to these situations, soon<br>
knew the pass I was brought to soon perceived my extreme disorder; in<br>
favour of which, removing the table out of the way, he began a prelude<br>
that flattered me with instant relief, to which I was not, however, so<br>
near as I imagined: for as he was unbuttoned to me, and tried to<br>
provoke and rouse to action his unactive torpid machine, he blushingly<br>
owned that no good was to be expected from it, unless I took it in hand<br>
to re-excite its languid loitering powers, by just refreshing the smart<br>
of the yet recent blood-raw cuts, seeing it could, no more than a boy&rsquo;s<br>
top, keep up without lashing. Sensible then that I should work as much<br>
for my own profit as his, I hurried my compliance with his desire, and<br>
abridging the ceremonial, whilst he leaned his head against the back of<br>
a chair, I had scarce gently made him feel the lash, before I saw the<br>
object of my wishes give signs of life, and presently, as it were with<br>
a magic touch, is started up into a noble size and distinction indeed.<br>
Hastening then to give me the benefit of it, he threw me down on the<br>
bench; but such was the refreshed soreness of those parts behind, on my<br>
leaning so hard on them, as became me to compass the admission of that<br>
stupendous head of his machine, that I could not possibly bear it. I<br>
got up then, and tried, by leaning forwards, and turning the crupper on<br>
my assailant, to let him at the back avenue: but here it was likewise<br>
impossible to stand his bearing so fiercely against me, in his<br>
agitations and endeavours to enter that way, whilst his belly battered<br>
directly against the recent sore. What should we do now? both<br>
intolerably heated: both in a fury; but pleasure is ever inventive for<br>
its own ends: he strips me in a trice stark naked, and placing a broad<br>
settee-cushion on the carpet before the fire, oversets me gently, topsy<br>
turvy, on it; and handling me only at the waist, whilst you may be sure<br>
I favoured all my dispositions, brought my legs round his neck; so that<br>
my head was kept from the floor only by my hands and the velvet<br>
cushion, which was now bespread with my flowing hair: thus I stood on<br>
my head and hands, supported by him in such manner, that whilst my<br>
thighs clung round him, so as to expose to his sight all my back<br>
figure, including the theatre of his bloody pleasure, the centre of my<br>
fore pair fairly bearded the object of its rage, that now stood in<br>
fine condition to give me satisfaction for the injuries of its<br>
neighbours. But as this posture was certainly not the easiest, and our<br>
imaginations, wound up to the height, could suffer no delay, he first,<br>
with the utmost eagerness and effort, just lip-lodged that broad<br>
acorn-fashioned head of his instrument; and still befriended by the<br>
fury with which he had made that impression, he soon stuffed in the<br>
rest; when now, with a pursuit of thrusts, fiercely urged, he<br>
absolutely overpowered and absorbed all sense of pain and uneasiness,<br>
whether from my wounds behind, my most untoward posture, or the<br>
oversize of his stretcher, in an infinitely predominant delight; when<br>
now all my whole spirits of life and sensation rushing, impetuously to<br>
the cock-pit, where the prize of pleasure was hotly in dispute and<br>
clustering to a point there, I soon received the dear relief of nature<br>
from these over-violent strains and provocations of it; harmonizing<br>
with which, my gallant spouted into me such a potent overflow of the<br>
