Charles, after a very short prelusive dalliance, lifting up my linen<br>
and his own, laid the broad treasures of his manly chest close to my<br>
bosom, both beating with the tenderest alarms: when now, the sense of<br>
his glowing body, in naked touch with mine, took all power over my<br>
thoughts out of my own disposal, and delivered up every faculty of the<br>
soul to the sensiblest of joys, that affecting me infinitely more with<br>
my distinction of the person, than of the sex, now brought my heart<br>
deliriously into play: my heart, which, eternally constant to Charles,<br>
had never taken any part in my original sacrifices to the calls of<br>
constitution, complaisance, or interest. But ah! what became of me,<br>
when as the powers of solid pleasure thickened upon me, I could not<br>
help feeling the stiff stake that had been adorned with the trophies of<br>
my despoiled virginity, bearing hard and inflexible against one of my<br>
thighs, which I had not yet opened, from a true principle of modesty,<br>
revived by a passion too sincere to suffer any aiming at the false<br>
merit of difficulty, or my putting on an impertinent mock coyness.<br>
<br>
I have, I believe, somewhere before remarked, that feel of that<br>
favourite piece of manhood has, in the very nature of it, something<br>
inimitably pathetic. Nothing can be dearer to the touch, nor can affect<br>
it with a more delirious sensation. Think then! as a love thinks, what<br>
must be the consummate transport of that quickest of our senses, in<br>
their central seat too! when, after so long a deprival, it felt itself<br>
re-inflamed under the pressure of that peculiar sceptre-member, which<br>
commands us all: but especially my darling, elect from the face of the<br>
whole earth. And now, at its mightiest point of stiffness, it felt to<br>
me something so subduing so active, so solid and agreeable, that I know<br>
not what name to give its singular impression: but the sentiment of<br>
consciousness of its belonging to my supremely beloved youth, gave me<br>
so pleasing an agitation, and worked so strongly on my soul, that it<br>
sent all its sensitive spirits to that organ of bliss in me, dedicated<br>
to its reception. There, concentering to a point, like rays in a<br>
burning glass, they glowed, they burnt with the intensest heat; the<br>
springs of pleasure were, in short, wound up to such a pitch, I panted<br>
now with so exquisitely keen an appetite for the eminent enjoyment,<br>
that I was even sick with desire, and unequal to support the<br>
combination of two distinct ideas, that delightfully distracted me: for<br>
all the thought I was capable of, was that I was now in touch, at once,<br>
with the instrument of pleasure, and the great seal of love. Ideas<br>
that, mingling streams, poured such an ocean of intoxicating bliss on a<br>
weak vessel, all too narrow to contain it, that I lay overwhelmed,<br>
absorbed, lost in an abyss of joy, and dying of nothing but immoderate<br>
delight.<br>
<br>
Charles then roused me somewhat out of this ecstatic distraction, with<br>
a complaint softly murmured, amidst a crowd of kisses, at the position,<br>
not so favourable to his desires, in which I received his urgent<br>
insistance for admission, where that insistance was alone so engrossing<br>
a pleasure, that it made me inconsistently suffer a much dearer one to<br>
be kept out; but how sweet to correct such a mistake! My thighs, now<br>
obedient to the intimations of love and nature, gladly disclose, and<br>
with a ready submission, resign up the soft gateway to the entrance of<br>
pleasure: I see, I feel the delicious velvet tip!... he enters me might<br>
and main, with... oh! my pen drops from here in the extasy now present<br>
to my faithful memory! Description too deserts me, and delivers over a<br>
task, above its strength of wing, to the imagination: but it must be an<br>
imagination exalted by such a flame as mine that can do justice to that<br>
sweetest, noblest of all sensations, that hailed and accompanied the<br>
stiff insinuation all the way up, till it was at the end of its<br>
penetration, sending up, through my eyes, the sparks of the love-fire<br>
that ran all over me and blazed in every vein and every pore of me; a<br>
system incarnate of joy all over.<br>
<br>
I had now totally taken in love&rsquo;s true arrow from the point up to the<br>
feather, in that part, where making no new wound, the lips or the<br>
original one of nature, which had owed its first breathing to this dear<br>
instrument, clung, as if sensible of gratitude, in eager suction round<br>
it, whilst all its inwards embraced it tenderly, with a warmth of gust,<br>
a compressive energy, that gave it, in its way, the heartiest welcome<br>
in nature; every fibre there gathering tight round it, and straining<br>
ambitiously to come in for its share of the blissful touch.<br>
<br>
As we were giving them a few moments pause to the the delectations of<br>
the senses, in dwelling with the highest relish on this intimatest<br>
point of re-union, and chewing the cud of enjoyment, the impatience<br>
natural to the pleasure soon drove us into action. Then began the<br>
driving tumult on his side, and the responsive heaves on mine, which<br>
kept me up to him; whilst, as our joys grew too great for utterance,<br>
the organs of our voices, voluptuously intermixing, became organs of<br>
the touch... how delicious!... how poignantly luscious!... And now! now<br>
I felt, to the heart of me! I felt the prodigious keen edge, with which<br>
love, presiding over this act, points the pleasure: love! that may be<br>
styled the Attic salt of enjoyment; and indeed, without it, the joy,<br>
great as it is, is still a vulgar one, whether in a king or a beggar;<br>
for it is, undoubtedly, love alone that refines, ennobles, and exalts<br>
it.<br>
<br>
Thus, happy, then, by the heart, happy by the senses, it was beyond all<br>
power, even of thought, to form the conception of a greater delight<br>
than what I now am consummating the fruition of.<br>
<br>
Charles, whose whole frame was convulsed with the agitation of his<br>
rapture, whilst the tenderest fires trembled in his eyes, all assured<br>
me of a perfect concord of joy, penetrated me so profoundly, touched me<br>
so vitally, took me so much out of my own possession, whilst he seemed<br>
himself so much in mine, that in a delicious enthusiasm, I imagined<br>
such a transfusion of heart and spirit, as that coalescing, and making<br>
one body and soul with him, I was he, and he me.<br>
<br>
But all this pleasure tending, like life from its first instants,<br>
towards its own dissolution, lived too fast not to bring on upon the<br>
spur its delicious moment of mortality; for presently the approach of<br>
the tender agony discovered itself by its usual signals, that were<br>
quickly followed by my dear lover&rsquo;s emanation of himself, that spun<br>
out, and shot, feelingly indeed! up the ravished indraught: where the<br>
sweetly soothing balmy titillation opened all the juices of joy on my<br>
side, which ecstatically in flow helped to allay the prurient glow, and<br>
drowned our pleasure for a while. Soon, however, to be on float again!<br>
for Charles, true to nature&rsquo;s laws, in one breath, expiring and<br>
ejaculating, languished not long in the dissolving trance, but<br>
recovering spirit again, soon gave me to feel that the true mettle<br>
spring! of his instrument of pleasure, were, by love, and perhaps, by a<br>
long vacation, wound up too high to be let down by a single explosion:<br>
his stiffnesss till stood my friend. Resuming then the action afresh,<br>
without dislodging, or giving me the trouble of parting from my sweet<br>
tenant, we played over again the same opera, with the same harmony and<br>
concert: our ardours, like our love, knew no remission; and all the<br>
tide serving my lover, lavish of his stores, and pleasure-milked, he<br>
over-flowed me once more from the fulness of his oval reservoirs of the<br>
genial emulsion: whilst, on my side, a convulsive grasp, in the instant<br>
of my giving down the liquid contribution, rendered me sweetly<br>
subservient at once to the increase of joy, and to its effusions:<br>
moving me so, as to make me exert all those springs of the compressive<br>
exsuction, with which the sensitive mechanism of that part thirstily<br>
draws and drains the nipple of Love; with much such an instinctive<br>
eagerness and attachment, as to compare great with less, kind nature<br>
engages infants at the breasts, by the pleasure they find in the motion<br>
of their little mouths and cheeks, to extract the milky stream prepared<br>
for their nourishment.<br>
<br>
But still there was no end of his vigour: this double discharge had so<br>
far from extinguished his desires, for that time, that it had not even<br>
calmed them; and at his age, desires are power. He was proceeding then<br>
amazingly to push it to a third triumph, still without uncasing, if a<br>
tenderness, natural to true love, had not inspired me with self-denial<br>
enough to spare, and not over-strain him: and accordingly, entreating<br>
him to give himself and me quarter, I obtained, at length, a short<br>
suspension of arms, but not before he had exultingly satisfied me that<br>
he gave out standing.<br>
<br>
The remainder of the night, with what we borrowed upon the day, we<br>
employed with unwearied fervour in celebrating thus the festival of our<br>
remeeting; and got up pretty late in the morning, gay, brisk and alert,<br>
though rest had been a stranger to us: but the pleasures of love had<br>
been to us, what the joy of victory is to an army: repose, refreshment,<br>
every thing.<br>
<br>
The journey into the country being now entirely out of the question,<br>
and orders having been given overnight for turning the horses&rsquo; heads<br>
towards London, we left the inn as soon as we had breakfasted, not<br>
without a liberal distribution of the tokens of my grateful sense of<br>
the happiness I had met with in it.<br>
<br>
Charles and I were in my coach; the captain and my companion in a<br>
chaise hired purposely for them, to leave us the conveniency of a<br>
_t&ecirc;te-&agrave;-t&ecirc;te_.<br>
<br>
Here, on the road, as the tumult of my senses was tolerably composed, I<br>
had command enough of head to break properly to his the course of life<br>
that the consequences of my separation from him had driven me into:<br>
which, at the same time that he tenderly deplored with me, he was the<br>
less shocked at; as, on reflecting how he had left me circumstances, he<br>
could not be entirely unprepared for it.<br>
<br>
But when I opened the state of my fortune to him, and with that<br>
sincerity which, from me to him, was so much a nature in me, I beged of<br>
him his acceptance of it, on his own terms. I should appear to you<br>
perhaps too partial to my passion, were I to attempt the doing his<br>
delicacy justice, I shall content myself then with assuring you, that<br>
after his flatly refusing the unreserved, unconditional donation that I<br>
long persecuted him in vain to accept, it was at length, in obedience<br>
to his serious commands (for I stood out unaffectedly, till he exerted<br>
the sovereign authority which love had given him over me), that I<br>
yielded my consent to waive the remonstrance I did not fail of making<br>
strongly to him, against his degrading himself, and incurring the<br>
reflection, however unjust, of having, for respects of fortune,<br>
bartered his honour for infamy and prostitution, in making one his<br>
wife, who thought herself too much honoured in being but his mistress.<br>
<br>
The plea of love then over-ruling all objections, for him, which he<br>
could not but read the sincerity of in a heart ever open to him,<br>
obliged me to receive his hand, by which means I was in pass, among<br>
other innumerable blessings, to bestow a legal parentage on those fine<br>
children you have seen by this happiest of matches.<br>
<br>
Thus, at length, I got snug into port, where, in the bosom of virtue, I<br>
gathered the only uncorrupt sweets: where, looking back on the course<br>
of vice I had run, and comparing its infamous blandishments with the<br>
infinitely superior joys of innocence, I could not help pitying, even<br>
in point of taste, those who, immersed in gross sensuality, are<br>
insensible to the so delicate charms of VIRTUE, than which even<br>
PLEASURE has not a greater friend, nor VICE a greater enemy. Thus<br>
temperance makes men lords over those pleasures that intemperance<br>
enslaves them to: the one, parent of health, vigour fertility<br>
cheerfulness, and every other desirable good of life; the other, of<br>
diseases, debility, barrenness, self-loathing, with only every evil<br>
incident to human nature.<br>
<br>
You laugh, perhaps, at this tail-piece of morality, extracted from me<br>
by the force of truth, resulting from compared experiences: you think<br>
it, no doubt, out of character; possibly too you may look on it as the<br>
paultry finesse of one who seeks to mask a devotee to vice under a rag<br>
of a veil, impudently smuggled from the shrine of Virtue: just as if<br>
one was to fancy one&rsquo;s self completely disguised at a masquerade, with<br>
no other change of dress than turning one&rsquo;s shoes into slippers; or, as<br>
if a writer should think to shield a treasonable libel, by concluding<br>
it with a formal prayer for the King. But, independent of my flattering<br>
myself that you have a juster opinion of my sense and sincerity, give<br>
me leave to represent to you, that such a supposition is even more<br>
injurious to Virtue than to me: since, consistently with candour and<br>
good nature, it san have no foundation but in the falsest of fears,<br>
that its pleasures cannot stand in comparison with those of Vice; but<br>
let truth dare to hold it up in its most alluring light: then mark, how<br>
spurious, how low of taste, how comparatively inferior its joys are to<br>
those which Virtue gives sanction to, and whose sentiments are not<br>
above making even a sauce for the senses, but a sauce of the highest<br>
relish; whilst Vices are the harpies that infect and foul the feast.<br>
The paths of Vice are sometimes strewed with roses, but then they are<br>
for ever infamous for many a thorn, for many a cankerworm: those of<br>
Virtue are strewed with roses purely, and those eternally unfading<br>
ones.<br>
<br>
If you do me then justice, you will esteem me perfectly consistent in<br>
the incense I burn to Virtue. If I have painted Vice in all its gayest<br>
colours, if I have decked it with flowers, it has been solely in order<br>
to make the worthier, the solemner sacrifice of it to Virtue.<br>
<br>
You know Mr. C*** O***, you know his estate, his worth, and good sense:<br>
can you, will you pronounce it ill meant, at least of him, when anxious<br>
for his son&rsquo;s morals, with a view to form him to virtue, and inspire<br>
him with a fixed, a rational contempt for vice, he condescended to be<br>
his master of the ceremonies, and led him by the hand through the most<br>
noted bawdy-houses in town, where he took care he should be<br>
familiarized with all those scenes of debauchery, so fit to nauseate a<br>
good taste? The experiment, you will cry, is dangerous. True, on a<br>
fool: but are fools worth so much attention.<br>
<br>
I shall see you soon, and in the mean time think candidly of me, and<br>
believe me ever,<br>
<br>
MADAM,<br>
Yours, etc., etc., etc.<br>
X X X<br>
<br>
THE END<br>
<br>
